Task instruction sent to agent 
# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Node.js Prototype Pollution Prevention in Core

## Your Task

Find all JavaScript source files in nodejs/node that defend against prototype pollution in core utilities: Object.create(null) usage, hasOwnProperty checks, and the safe merge/assign patterns used in core modules.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of JavaScript source files in nodejs/node that defend against prototype pollution. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Prototype Pollution Defense Patterns Found

**1. Safe Built-in Collections** (`lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js`)
- `SafeMap`, `SafeWeakMap`, `SafeSet`, `SafeWeakSet` - created with frozen null prototypes
- `makeSafe()` function that creates prototype-safe versions of built-ins

**2. Null-Prototype Objects**
- Widespread use of `{ __proto__: null }` pattern throughout core modules
- `kEmptyObject` constant in `lib/internal/util.js` (line 733)
- Used in query parsing, error handling, HTTP/2 headers, test runners, and more

**3. ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty Checks**
- Prevents trusting hasOwnProperty on user objects
- Used in crypto utilities, buffer operations, validators, and object inspection
- Prevents inherited properties from bypassing security checks

**4. Safe Merge/Assign Patterns**
- `filterOwnProperties()` function creates null-prototype filtered objects
- `setOwnProperty()` function uses ObjectDefineProperty with safe descriptors
- Explicit hasOwnProperty checks in for-in loops

**5. Property Descriptor Defense**
- All property descriptors use `__proto__: null`
- Prevents pollution through Object.defineProperty

**39 files examined** containing these defensive patterns, with 13 key symbols identified that implement prototype pollution defense mechanisms.

The analysis has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings about files, symbols, and the implementation chain used to defend against prototype pollution.
